     <div class="mw-parser-output">
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       This article is about the country. For the archipelago, see <a href="/wiki/Comoro_Islands" title="Comoro Islands">Comoro Islands</a>.
      </div>

       Federal republic in the Indian Ocean

      <p>The <b>Comoros</b>,<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[nb 1]</a></sup> officially the <b>Union of the Comoros</b>,<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[nb 2]</a></sup> is an island country in the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Ocean" title="Indian Ocean">Indian Ocean</a>, at the northern end of the <a href="/wiki/Mozambique_Channel" title="Mozambique Channel">Mozambique Channel</a> off the eastern coast of Africa. It shares maritime borders with <a href="/wiki/Madagascar" title="Madagascar">Madagascar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mayotte" title="Mayotte">Mayotte</a> to the southeast, <a href="/wiki/Tanzania" title="Tanzania">Tanzania</a> to the northwest, <a href="/wiki/Mozambique" title="Mozambique">Mozambique</a> to the west, and the <a href="/wiki/Seychelles" title="Seychelles">Seychelles</a> to the northeast. Its capital and largest city is <a href="/wiki/Moroni,_Comoros" title="Moroni, Comoros">Moroni</a>. The religion of the majority of the population, and the official state religion, is Sunni Islam. As a member of the <a href="/wiki/Arab_League" title="Arab League">Arab League</a>, it is the only country in the <a href="/wiki/Arab_world" title="Arab world">Arab world</a> which is entirely in the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Hemisphere" title="Southern Hemisphere">Southern Hemisphere</a>. It is also a member state of the <a href="/wiki/African_Union" title="African Union">African Union</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_internationale_de_la_Francophonie" title="Organisation internationale de la Francophonie">Organisation internationale de la Francophonie</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_of_Islamic_Cooperation" title="Organisation of Islamic Cooperation">Organisation of Islamic Cooperation</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Ocean_Commission" title="Indian Ocean Commission">Indian Ocean Commission</a>. The country has three official languages: <a href="/wiki/Comorian_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Comorian language">Comorian</a>, <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>. </p>
      <p>At 1,861&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (719&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi), excluding the contested island of Mayotte, the Comoros is the fourth-smallest African nation by area. Its population, excluding Mayotte, is estimated at 832,322 as of 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-7">[5]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_2019_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP_2019-8">[6]</a></sup> As a nation formed at a crossroads of different civilisations, the <a href="/wiki/Archipelago" title="Archipelago">archipelago</a> is noted for its diverse culture and history. </p>
      <p>The sovereign state consists of three major islands and numerous smaller islands, all in the volcanic <a href="/wiki/Comoro_Islands" title="Comoro Islands">Comoro Islands</a>. The major islands are commonly known by their French names: northwesternmost <a href="/wiki/Grande_Comore" title="Grande Comore">Grande Comore</a> (Ngazidja), <a href="/wiki/Moh%C3%A9li" title="Mohéli">Mohéli</a> (Mwali), and <a href="/wiki/Anjouan" title="Anjouan">Anjouan</a> (Ndzuani). The country also claims a fourth major island, southeasternmost Mayotte (Maore), though Mayotte voted against independence from France in 1974, since it has never been administered by an independent Comoros government, and continues to be administered by France as an <a href="/wiki/Overseas_department" class="mw-redirect" title="Overseas department">overseas department</a>. France has vetoed <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">United Nations Security Council</a> <a href="/wiki/List_of_Vetoed_United_Nation_Security_Council_Resolutions" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Vetoed United Nation Security Council Resolutions">resolutions</a> that would affirm Comorian sovereignty over the island.<sup id="cite_ref-GA31_first-resolution_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GA31_first-resolution-9">[7]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[8]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-GlobalPolicy_SC-Vetoes_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GlobalPolicy_SC-Vetoes-11">[9]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-article33_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-article33-12">[10]</a></sup> In addition, Mayotte became an overseas department and a region of France in 2011 following a referendum passed overwhelmingly. </p>
      <p>Comoros was first settled by <a href="/wiki/Bantu_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Bantu language">Bantu</a> speakers from East Africa, Arabs, and <a href="/wiki/Austronesian_languages" title="Austronesian languages">Austronesians</a>. It then became part of the <a href="/wiki/French_colonial_empire" title="French colonial empire">French colonial empire</a> during the 19th century, before its independence in 1975. Since then, it has experienced more than 20 coups or attempted coups, with various heads of state assassinated.<sup id="cite_ref-20Coups_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20Coups-13">[11]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[12]</a></sup> Along with this constant political instability, it has the worst <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_income_equality" title="List of countries by income equality">income inequality</a> of any nation, with a <a href="/wiki/Gini_coefficient" title="Gini coefficient">Gini coefficient</a> over 60%, and ranks in the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_Human_Development_Index#Low_human_development" title="List of countries by Human Development Index">worst quartile</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a>. As of 2008<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Comoros&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, about half the population lived below the <a href="/wiki/International_poverty_line" class="mw-redirect" title="International poverty line">international poverty line</a> of US$1.25 a day.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[13]</a></sup> The French insular region of Mayotte, the most prosperous territory in the Mozambique Channel, is a major destination for <a href="/wiki/Human_migration" title="Human migration">migrants</a> from the independent islands. </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comoros&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>The name "Comoros" derives from the Arabic word <span lang="ar" title="Arabic-language text"><big><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%D9%82%D9%85%D8%B1#Noun" class="extiw" title="wikt:قمر">قمر</a></big></span> <i>qamar</i> ("<a href="/wiki/Moon" title="Moon">moon</a>").<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[14]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comoros&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Comoros" title="History of the Comoros">History of the Comoros</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Settlement">Settlement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comoros&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Settlement">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Vanilla_plantation_in_wood_dsc00190.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Vanilla_plantation_in_wood_dsc00190.jpg/170px-Vanilla_plantation_in_wood_dsc00190.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Vanilla_plantation_in_wood_dsc00190.jpg/255px-Vanilla_plantation_in_wood_dsc00190.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Vanilla_plantation_in_wood_dsc00190.jpg/340px-Vanilla_plantation_in_wood_dsc00190.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1728" data-file-height="2592"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Vanilla_plantation_in_wood_dsc00190.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A <a href="/wiki/Vanilla" title="Vanilla">vanilla</a> plantation
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>According to mythology, a <a href="/wiki/Jinn" title="Jinn">jinni</a> (spirit) dropped a <a href="/wiki/Gemstone" title="Gemstone">jewel</a>, which formed a great circular inferno. This became the <a href="/wiki/Mount_Karthala" title="Mount Karthala">Karthala volcano</a>, which created the island of Grande Comoro. King Solomon is also said to have visited the island. </p>
      <p>The first attested human inhabitants of the Comoro Islands are now thought to have been <a href="/wiki/Austronesian_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Austronesian people">Austronesian</a> settlers travelling by boat from <a href="/wiki/Island_Southeast_Asia" class="mw-redirect" title="Island Southeast Asia">islands in Southeast Asia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[15]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[16]</a></sup> These people arrived no later than the eighth century AD, the date of the earliest known <a href="/wiki/Archaeological" class="mw-redirect" title="Archaeological">archaeological</a> site, found on <a href="/wiki/Mayotte" title="Mayotte">Mayotte</a>, although settlement beginning as early as the first century has been postulated.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[17]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Subsequent settlers came from the east coast of Africa, the Arabian Peninsula and the <a href="/wiki/Persian_Gulf" title="Persian Gulf">Persian Gulf</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Malay_Archipelago" title="Malay Archipelago">Malay Archipelago</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Madagascar" title="Madagascar">Madagascar</a>. <a href="/wiki/Bantu_languages" title="Bantu languages">Bantu</a>-speaking settlers were present on the islands from the beginnings of settlement, probably brought to the islands as slaves.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[18]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Development of the Comoros is divided into phases. The earliest reliably recorded phase is the Dembeni phase (eighth to tenth centuries), during which there were several small settlements on each island.<sup id="cite_ref-spear_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-spear-21">[19]</a></sup> From the eleventh to the fifteenth centuries, trade with the island of Madagascar and merchants from the Swahili coast and the <a href="/wiki/Middle_East" title="Middle East">Middle East</a> flourished, more villages were founded and existing villages grew. Many Comorians can trace their genealogies to ancestors from the Arabian peninsula, particularly <a href="/wiki/Hadhramaut" title="Hadhramaut">Hadhramaut</a>, who arrived during this period. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Medieval_Comoros">Medieval Comoros</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comoros&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Medieval Comoros">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>According to legend, in 632, upon hearing of <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a>, islanders are said to have dispatched an emissary, Mtswa-Mwindza, to <a href="/wiki/Mecca" title="Mecca">Mecca</a>—but by the time he arrived there, the Prophet <a href="/wiki/Muhammad" title="Muhammad">Muhammad</a> had died. Nonetheless, after a stay in Mecca, he returned to Ngazidja and led the gradual conversion of his islanders to Islam.<sup id="cite_ref-verin_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-verin-22">[20]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Among the earliest accounts of East Africa, the works of <a href="/wiki/Al-Masudi" title="Al-Masudi">Al-Masudi</a> describe early Islamic trade routes, and how the coast and islands were frequently visited by <a href="/wiki/Muslim" class="mw-redirect" title="Muslim">Muslims</a> including <a href="/wiki/Persia" class="mw-redirect" title="Persia">Persian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arab" class="mw-redirect" title="Arab">Arab</a> merchants and sailors in search of <a href="/wiki/Coral" title="Coral">coral</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ambergris" title="Ambergris">ambergris</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ivory" title="Ivory">ivory</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tortoiseshell" title="Tortoiseshell">tortoiseshell</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gold" title="Gold">gold</a> and slaves. They also brought Islam to the people of the <a href="/wiki/Zanj" title="Zanj">Zanj</a> including the Comoros. As the importance of the Comoros grew along the East African coast, both small and large <a href="/wiki/Mosque" title="Mosque">mosques</a> were constructed. The Comoros are part of the <a href="/wiki/Swahili_Coast" class="mw-redirect" title="Swahili Coast">Swahili</a> cultural and economic complex and the islands became a major hub of trade and an important location in a network of trading towns that included <a href="/wiki/Kilwa_Kisiwani" title="Kilwa Kisiwani">Kilwa</a>, in present-day Tanzania, Sofala (an outlet for <a href="/wiki/Zimbabwe" title="Zimbabwe">Zimbabwean</a> gold), in <a href="/wiki/Mozambique" title="Mozambique">Mozambique</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mombasa" title="Mombasa">Mombasa</a> in <a href="/wiki/Kenya" title="Kenya">Kenya</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-spear_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-spear-21">[19]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Portuguese arrived in the Indian Ocean at the end of the 15th century and the first Portuguese visit to the islands seems to have been that of Vasco da Gama's second fleet in 1503.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[21]</a></sup> For much of the 16th century the islands provided provisions to the Portuguese fort at Mozambique and although there was no formal attempt by the Portuguese crown to take possession, a number of Portuguese traders settled. </p>
      <p>By the end of the 16th century the local rulers were beginning to push back and, with the support of the Omani Sultan <a href="/wiki/Saif_bin_Sultan" title="Saif bin Sultan">Saif bin Sultan</a> they began to defeat the Dutch and the Portuguese. His successor <a href="/wiki/Said_bin_Sultan,_Sultan_of_Muscat_and_Oman" class="mw-redirect" title="Said bin Sultan, Sultan of Muscat and Oman">Said bin Sultan</a> increased Omani Arab influence in the region, moving his administration to nearby <a href="/wiki/Zanzibar" title="Zanzibar">Zanzibar</a>, which came under <a href="/wiki/Oman" title="Oman">Omani</a> rule. Nevertheless, the Comoros remained independent, and although the three smaller islands were usually politically unified, the largest island, Ngazidja, was divided into a number of autonomous kingdoms (<i>ntsi</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-Thomas_Spear_1984_291–305_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thomas_Spear_1984_291–305-24">[22]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>By the time Europeans showed interest in the Comoros, the islanders were well placed to take advantage of their needs, initially supplying ships of the route to India, particularly the English and, later, slaves to the plantation islands in the <a href="/wiki/Mascarene_Islands" title="Mascarene Islands">Mascarenes</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[23]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Thomas_Spear_1984_291–305_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thomas_Spear_1984_291–305-24">[22]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="European_contact_and_French_colonisation">European contact and French colonisation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comoros&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: European contact and French colonisation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Carte_des_isles_de_Comore_Johanna_ou_Anjouan_Mohilla_ou_Moaly_et_Mayote_Bnf40600530t.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Carte_des_isles_de_Comore_Johanna_ou_Anjouan_Mohilla_ou_Moaly_et_Mayote_Bnf40600530t.jpg/220px-Carte_des_isles_de_Comore_Johanna_ou_Anjouan_Mohilla_ou_Moaly_et_Mayote_Bnf40600530t.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="203" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Carte_des_isles_de_Comore_Johanna_ou_Anjouan_Mohilla_ou_Moaly_et_Mayote_Bnf40600530t.jpg/330px-Carte_des_isles_de_Comore_Johanna_ou_Anjouan_Mohilla_ou_Moaly_et_Mayote_Bnf40600530t.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Carte_des_isles_de_Comore_Johanna_ou_Anjouan_Mohilla_ou_Moaly_et_Mayote_Bnf40600530t.jpg/440px-Carte_des_isles_de_Comore_Johanna_ou_Anjouan_Mohilla_ou_Moaly_et_Mayote_Bnf40600530t.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1140" data-file-height="1054"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Carte_des_isles_de_Comore_Johanna_ou_Anjouan_Mohilla_ou_Moaly_et_Mayote_Bnf40600530t.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>French map of the Comores, 1747
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Map_of_Africa_(1808)_-_CAMORA_excerpt.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/47/Map_of_Africa_%281808%29_-_CAMORA_excerpt.jpg/220px-Map_of_Africa_%281808%29_-_CAMORA_excerpt.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="151" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/47/Map_of_Africa_%281808%29_-_CAMORA_excerpt.jpg/330px-Map_of_Africa_%281808%29_-_CAMORA_excerpt.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/4/47/Map_of_Africa_%281808%29_-_CAMORA_excerpt.jpg 2x" data-file-width="341" data-file-height="234"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Map_of_Africa_(1808)_-_CAMORA_excerpt.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>An 1808 map refers to the islands as "Camora".
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Moroni-Place_des_Assembl%C3%A9es.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Moroni-Place_des_Assembl%C3%A9es.jpg/220px-Moroni-Place_des_Assembl%C3%A9es.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="143" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Moroni-Place_des_Assembl%C3%A9es.jpg/330px-Moroni-Place_des_Assembl%C3%A9es.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Moroni-Place_des_Assembl%C3%A9es.jpg/440px-Moroni-Place_des_Assembl%C3%A9es.jpg 2x" data-file-width="671" data-file-height="435"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Moroni-Place_des_Assembl%C3%A9es.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A public square, Moroni, 1908
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In the last decade of the 18th century, Malagasy warriors, mostly Betsimisaraka and Sakalava, started raiding the Comoros for <a href="/wiki/Slave" class="mw-redirect" title="Slave">slaves</a> and the islands were devastated as crops were destroyed and the people were slaughtered, taken into captivity or fled to the African mainland: it is said that by the time the raids finally ended in the second decade of the 19th century only one man remained on Mwali.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[24]</a></sup> The islands were repopulated by slaves from the mainland, who were traded to the French in Mayotte and the Mascarenes. On the Comoros, it was estimated in 1865 that as much as 40% of the population consisted of slaves.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[25]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>France first established colonial rule in the Comoros by taking possession of Mayotte in 1841 when the <a href="/wiki/Sakalava_people" title="Sakalava people">Sakalava</a> usurper sultan <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andriantsoly&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Andriantsoly (page does not exist)">Andriantsoly</a></i> (also known as Tsy Levalo) signed the Treaty of April 1841,<sup id="cite_ref-Encyclopaedia_of_Islam_1979,_vol._v,_p._381_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclopaedia_of_Islam_1979,_vol._v,_p._381-28">[26]</a></sup> which ceded the island to the French authorities.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[27]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Meanwhile, Ndzuani (or Johanna as it was know to the British) continued to serve as a way station for English merchants sailing to India and the Far East, as well as American whalers, although the British gradually abandoned it following their possession of Mauritius in 1814 and by the time the <a href="/wiki/Suez_Canal" title="Suez Canal">Suez Canal</a> opened in 1869 there was no longer any significant supply trade at Ndzuani. Local commodities exported by the Comoros were, in addition to slaves, coconuts, timber, cattle and tortoiseshell. French settlers, French-owned companies, and wealthy Arab merchants established a plantation-based economy that used about one-third of the land for export crops. After its annexation, France converted Mayotte into a sugar plantation colony. The other islands were soon transformed as well, and the major crops of ylang-ylang, vanilla, cloves, perfume plants, coffee,cocoa beans, and sisal were introduced.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[28]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 1886, Mwali was placed under French protection by its Sultan Mardjani Abdou Cheikh. That same year, Sultan Said Ali of <a href="/wiki/Sultanate_of_Bambao" title="Sultanate of Bambao">Bambao</a>, one of the sultanates on Ngazidja, placed the island under French protection in exchange for French support of his claim to the entire island, which he retained until his abdication in 1910. In 1908 the islands were unified under a single administration (<i>Colonie de Mayotte et dépendances</i>) and placed under the authority of the French colonial governor general of Madagascar. In 1909, Sultan Said Muhamed of Ndzuani abdicated in favour of French rule. In 1912 the colony and the protectorates were abolished and the islands became a province of the colony of Madagascar.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[29]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Agreement was reached with France in 1973 for the Comoros to become independent in 1978, despite the deputies of <a href="/wiki/Mayotte" title="Mayotte">Mayotte</a> voting for increased integration with France. A referendum was held on all four of the islands. Three voted for independence by large margins, while Mayotte voted against, and remains under French administration. On 6 July 1975, however, the Comorian parliament passed a unilateral resolution declaring independence. Ahmed Abdallah proclaimed the independence of the Comorian State (<i>État comorien</i>; دولة القمر) and became its first president. The French recognised the new state. </p> 
      <h3><span id="Independence_.281975.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Independence_(1975)">Independence (1975)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comoros&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Independence (1975)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_the_Comoros_(1963%E2%80%931975).svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Flag_of_the_Comoros_%281963%E2%80%931975%29.svg/220px-Flag_of_the_Comoros_%281963%E2%80%931975%29.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Flag_of_the_Comoros_%281963%E2%80%931975%29.svg/330px-Flag_of_the_Comoros_%281963%E2%80%931975%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Flag_of_the_Comoros_%281963%E2%80%931975%29.svg/440px-Flag_of_the_Comoros_%281963%E2%80%931975%29.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="800"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">

         </div><a href="/wiki/Flag_of_the_Comoros" title="Flag of the Comoros">Flag of the Comoros</a> (1963 to 1975)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_the_Comoros_(1975%E2%80%931978).svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Flag_of_the_Comoros_%281975%E2%80%931978%29.svg/220px-Flag_of_the_Comoros_%281975%E2%80%931978%29.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="157" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Flag_of_the_Comoros_%281975%E2%80%931978%29.svg/330px-Flag_of_the_Comoros_%281975%E2%80%931978%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Flag_of_the_Comoros_%281975%E2%80%931978%29.svg/440px-Flag_of_the_Comoros_%281975%E2%80%931978%29.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="840" data-file-height="600"></a>

         </div><a href="/wiki/Flag_of_the_Comoros" title="Flag of the Comoros">Flag of the Comoros</a> (1975 to 1978)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Ikililou_Dhoinine_2012.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Ikililou_Dhoinine_2012.jpg/170px-Ikililou_Dhoinine_2012.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="201" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Ikililou_Dhoinine_2012.jpg/255px-Ikililou_Dhoinine_2012.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Ikililou_Dhoinine_2012.jpg/340px-Ikililou_Dhoinine_2012.jpg 2x" data-file-width="701" data-file-height="827"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Ikililou_Dhoinine_2012.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Ikililou_Dhoinine" title="Ikililou Dhoinine">Ikililou Dhoinine</a>, <a href="/wiki/President_of_Comoros" class="mw-redirect" title="President of Comoros">President of Comoros</a> from 2011 to 2016
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The next 30 years were a period of political turmoil. On 3 August 1975, less than one month after independence, president <a href="/wiki/Ahmed_Abdallah" title="Ahmed Abdallah">Ahmed Abdallah</a> was removed from office in an armed coup and replaced with United National Front of the Comoros (FNUK) member Prince <a href="/wiki/Said_Mohamed_Jaffar" title="Said Mohamed Jaffar">Said Mohamed Jaffar</a>. Months later, in January 1976, Jaffar was ousted in favour of his Minister of Defense <a href="/wiki/Ali_Soilih" title="Ali Soilih">Ali Soilih</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Mukonoweshuro:555-577_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mukonoweshuro:555-577-32">[30]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The population of <a href="/wiki/Mayotte" title="Mayotte">Mayotte</a> voted against independence from France in three referenda during this period. The <a href="/wiki/1974_Comorian_independence_referendum" title="1974 Comorian independence referendum">first</a>, held on all the islands on 22 December 1974, won 63.8% support for maintaining ties with France on Mayotte; the <a href="/wiki/1976_Mahoran_status_referendum" title="1976 Mahoran status referendum">second</a>, held in February 1976, confirmed that vote with an overwhelming 99.4%, while the third, in April 1976, confirmed that the people of Mayotte wished to remain a French territory. The three remaining islands, ruled by President Soilih, instituted a number of socialist and isolationist policies that soon strained relations with France. On 13 May 1978, <a href="/wiki/Bob_Denard" title="Bob Denard">Bob Denard</a> returned to overthrow President Soilih and reinstate Abdallah with the support of the French, Rhodesian and South African governments. During Soilih's brief rule, he faced seven additional coup attempts until he was finally forced from office and killed.<sup id="cite_ref-Mukonoweshuro:555-577_32-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mukonoweshuro:555-577-32">[30]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[31]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In contrast to Soilih, Abdallah's presidency was marked by authoritarian rule and increased adherence to traditional Islam<sup id="cite_ref-Bakar:181-191_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bakar:181-191-34">[32]</a></sup> and the country was renamed the Federal <a href="/wiki/Islamic_Republic" class="mw-redirect" title="Islamic Republic">Islamic Republic</a> of the Comoros (<i>République Fédérale Islamique des Comores</i>; جمهورية القمر الإتحادية الإسلامية). Abdallah continued as president until 1989 when, fearing a probable coup, he signed a decree ordering the Presidential Guard, led by Bob Denard, to disarm the armed forces. Shortly after the signing of the decree, Abdallah was allegedly shot dead in his office by a disgruntled military officer, though later sources claim an antitank missile was launched into his bedroom and killed him.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[33]</a></sup> Although Denard was also injured, it is suspected that Abdallah's killer was a soldier under his command.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[34]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>A few days later, Bob Denard was evacuated to South Africa by French paratroopers. <a href="/wiki/Said_Mohamed_Djohar" title="Said Mohamed Djohar">Said Mohamed Djohar</a>, Soilih's older half-brother, then became president, and served until September 1995, when Bob Denard returned and attempted another coup. This time France intervened with paratroopers and forced Denard to surrender.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[35]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[36]</a></sup> The French removed Djohar to Reunion, and the Paris-backed <a href="/wiki/Mohamed_Taki_Abdoulkarim" title="Mohamed Taki Abdoulkarim">Mohamed Taki Abdoulkarim</a> became president by election. He led the country from 1996, during a time of labour crises, government suppression, and secessionist conflicts, until his death November 1998. He was succeeded by Interim President <a href="/wiki/Tadjidine_Ben_Said_Massounde" title="Tadjidine Ben Said Massounde">Tadjidine Ben Said Massounde</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[37]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The islands of <a href="/wiki/Anjouan" title="Anjouan">Ndzuani</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mwali" class="mw-redirect" title="Mwali">Mwali</a> declared their independence from the Comoros in 1997, in an attempt to restore French rule. But France rejected their request, leading to bloody confrontations between federal troops and rebels.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[38]</a></sup> In April 1999, Colonel <a href="/wiki/Azali_Assoumani" title="Azali Assoumani">Azali Assoumani</a>, Army Chief of Staff, seized power in a bloodless coup, overthrowing the Interim President Massounde, citing weak leadership in the face of the crisis. This was the Comoros' 18th coup, or attempted coup d'état since independence in 1975.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[39]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Azali failed to consolidate power and reestablish control over the islands, which was the subject of international criticism. The <a href="/wiki/African_Union" title="African Union">African Union</a>, under the auspices of President <a href="/wiki/Thabo_Mbeki" title="Thabo Mbeki">Thabo Mbeki</a> of South Africa, imposed sanctions on Ndzuani to help broker negotiations and effect reconciliation.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[40]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[41]</a></sup> Under the terms of the Fomboni Accords, signed in December 2001 by the leaders of all three islands, the official name of the country was changed to the Union of the Comoros; the new state was to be highly decentralised and the central union government would devolve most powers to the new island governments, each lead by a president. The Union president, although elected by national elections, would be chosen in rotation from each of the islands every five years. </p>
      <p>Azali stepped down in 2002 to run in the democratic election of the President of the Comoros, which he won. Under ongoing international pressure, as a military ruler who had originally come to power by force, and was not always democratic while in office, Azali led the Comoros through constitutional changes that enabled new elections.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[42]</a></sup> A <i>Loi des compétences</i> law was passed in early 2005 that defines the responsibilities of each governmental body, and is in the process of implementation. The elections in 2006 were won by <a href="/wiki/Ahmed_Abdallah_Mohamed_Sambi" title="Ahmed Abdallah Mohamed Sambi">Ahmed Abdallah Mohamed Sambi</a>, a Sunni Muslim cleric nicknamed the "Ayatollah" for his time spent studying Islam in Iran. Azali honoured the election results, thus allowing the first peaceful and democratic exchange of power for the archipelago.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[43]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Colonel <a href="/wiki/Mohammed_Bacar" class="mw-redirect" title="Mohammed Bacar">Mohammed Bacar</a>, a French-trained former gendarme elected President of Ndzuani in 2001, refused to step down at the end of his five-year mandate. He staged a vote in June 2007 to confirm his leadership that was rejected as illegal by the Comoros federal government and the African Union. On 25 March 2008 hundreds of soldiers from the African Union and the Comoros seized rebel-held Ndzuani, generally welcomed by the population: there have been reports of hundreds, if not thousands, of people tortured during Bacar's tenure.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[44]</a></sup> Some rebels were killed and injured, but there are no official figures. At least 11 civilians were wounded. Some officials were imprisoned. Bacar fled in a speedboat to the French Indian Ocean territory of Mayotte to seek asylum. Anti-French protests followed in the Comoros (see <a href="/wiki/2008_invasion_of_Anjouan" title="2008 invasion of Anjouan">2008 invasion of Anjouan</a>). Bacar was eventually granted asylum in Benin. </p>
      <p>Since independence from France, the Comoros experienced more than 20 coups or attempted coups.<sup id="cite_ref-20Coups_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20Coups-13">[11]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Following elections in late 2010, former Vice-President <a href="/wiki/Ikililou_Dhoinine" title="Ikililou Dhoinine">Ikililou Dhoinine</a> was inaugurated as president on 26 May 2011. A member of the ruling party, Dhoinine was supported in the election by the incumbent President Ahmed Abdallah Mohamed Sambi. Dhoinine, a pharmacist by training, is the first President of the Comoros from the island of Mwali. Following the 2016 elections, <a href="/wiki/Azali_Assoumani" title="Azali Assoumani">Azali Assoumani</a>, from Ngazidja, became president for a third term. In 2018 Azali held a referendum on constitutional reform that would permit a president to serve two terms. The amendments passed, although the vote was widely contested and boycotted by the opposition, and in April 2019, and to widespread opposition, Azali was re-elected president to serve the first of potentially two five-year terms. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comoros&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <table class="box-Unreferenced_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation">
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <td class="mbox-image">
          <div style="width:52px">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399"></a>
          </div></td>
         <td class="mbox-text">
          <div class="mbox-text-span">
           This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Comoros&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Referencing_for_beginners" title="Help:Referencing for beginners">adding citations to reliable sources</a>.
