          </div></td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_the_Comoros" title="Geography of the Comoros">Geography of the Comoros</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Cn-map.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Cn-map.png/300px-Cn-map.png" decoding="async" width="300" height="323" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/e3/Cn-map.png 1.5x" data-file-width="330" data-file-height="355"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Cn-map.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A map of the Comoros
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Comoros is formed by <a href="/wiki/Grande_Comore" title="Grande Comore">Ngazidja</a> (Grande Comore), <a href="/wiki/Moh%C3%A9li" title="Mohéli">Mwali</a> (Mohéli) and <a href="/wiki/Anjouan" title="Anjouan">Ndzuani</a> (Anjouan), three major islands in the Comoros Archipelago, as well as many minor islets. The islands are officially known by their Comorian language names, though international sources still use their French names (given in parentheses above). The capital and largest city, <a href="/wiki/Moroni,_Comoros" title="Moroni, Comoros">Moroni</a>, is located on Ngazidja. The archipelago is situated in the Indian Ocean, in the <a href="/wiki/Mozambique_Channel" title="Mozambique Channel">Mozambique Channel</a>, between the African coast (nearest to <a href="/wiki/Mozambique" title="Mozambique">Mozambique</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tanzania" title="Tanzania">Tanzania</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Madagascar" title="Madagascar">Madagascar</a>, with no land borders. </p>
      <p>At 1,861&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (719&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi), it is one of the smallest countries in the world. The Comoros also has claim to 320&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (120&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi) of territorial seas. The interiors of the islands vary from steep mountains to low hills. </p>
      <p>The areas and populations (at the 2017 Census) of the main islands are as follows:<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-47">[45]</a></sup> </p> 
      <table class="sortable wikitable"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr> 
         <th>Name</th> 
         <th>Area <br>km<sup>2</sup></th> 
         <th>Population<br>Census 2017<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_47-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-47">[45]</a></sup> </th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td>Mwali</td> 
         <td align="right">290</td> 
         <td align="right">51,567 </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td>Njazidja</td> 
         <td align="right">1,147</td> 
         <td align="right">379,367 </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td>Nzwani</td> 
         <td align="right">424</td> 
         <td align="right">327,382 </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><i><b>Totals</b></i></td> 
         <td align="right">1,861</td> 
         <td align="right">758,316 </td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <p>Ngazidja is the largest of the Comoros Archipelago, with an area of 1,147&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup>. It is also the most recent island, and therefore has rocky soil. The island's two volcanoes, <a href="/wiki/Mount_Karthala" title="Mount Karthala">Karthala</a> (active) and <a href="/wiki/La_Grille" title="La Grille">La Grille</a> (dormant), and the lack of good harbours are distinctive characteristics of its terrain. Mwali, with its capital at <a href="/wiki/Fomboni" title="Fomboni">Fomboni</a>, is the smallest of the four major islands. Ndzuani, whose capital is <a href="/wiki/Mutsamudu" title="Mutsamudu">Mutsamudu</a>, has a distinctive triangular shape caused by three mountain chains – <a href="/wiki/Sima,_Comoros" title="Sima, Comoros">Shisiwani</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Nioumakele&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Nioumakele (page does not exist)">Nioumakele</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jimilime" class="mw-redirect" title="Jimilime">Jimilime</a> – emanating from a central peak, Mount <a href="/w/index.php?title=Ntingui&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Ntingui (page does not exist)">Ntingui</a> (1,575&nbsp;m or 5,167&nbsp;ft). </p>
      <p>The islands of the Comoros Archipelago were formed by volcanic activity. Mount Karthala, an active <a href="/wiki/Shield_volcano" title="Shield volcano">shield volcano</a> located on Ngazidja, is the country's highest point, at 2,361 metres (7,746 feet). It contains the Comoros' largest patch of disappearing rainforest. Karthala is currently one of the most active volcanoes in the world, with a minor eruption in May 2006, and prior eruptions as recently as April 2005 and 1991. In the 2005 eruption, which lasted from 17 to 19 April, 40,000 citizens were evacuated, and the <a href="/wiki/Volcanic_crater_lake" title="Volcanic crater lake">crater lake</a> in the volcano's 3 by 4 kilometres (1.9 by 2.5 miles) <a href="/wiki/Caldera" title="Caldera">caldera</a> was destroyed. </p>
      <p>The Comoros also lays claim to the <a href="/wiki/Scattered_Islands_in_the_Indian_Ocean" title="Scattered Islands in the Indian Ocean"><i>Îles Éparses</i> or <i>Îles éparses de l'océan indien</i></a> (Scattered Islands in the Indian Ocean) – <a href="/wiki/Glorioso_Islands" title="Glorioso Islands">Glorioso Islands</a>, comprising <a href="/wiki/Grande_Glorieuse" class="mw-redirect" title="Grande Glorieuse">Grande Glorieuse</a>, <a href="/wiki/%C3%8Ele_du_Lys" title="Île du Lys">Île du Lys</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Wreck_Rock&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Wreck Rock (page does not exist)">Wreck Rock</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=South_Rock&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="South Rock (page does not exist)">South Rock</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Verte_Rocks&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Verte Rocks (page does not exist)">Verte Rocks</a> (three islets) and three unnamed islets – one of France's overseas districts. The Glorioso Islands were administered by the colonial Comoros before 1975, and are therefore sometimes considered part of the Comoros Archipelago. <a href="/wiki/Banc_du_Geyser" title="Banc du Geyser">Banc du Geyser</a>, a former island in the Comoros Archipelago, now submerged, is geographically located in the <i>Îles Éparses</i>, but was annexed by <a href="/wiki/Madagascar" title="Madagascar">Madagascar</a> in 1976 as an unclaimed territory. The Comoros and France each still view the Banc du Geyser as part of the Glorioso Islands and, thus, part of its particular exclusive economic zone. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comoros&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Moroni,_Comoros#Geography_and_climate" title="Moroni, Comoros">Moroni, Comoros §&nbsp;Geography and climate</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The climate is generally tropical and mild, and the two major seasons are distinguishable by their raininess. The temperature reaches an average of 29–30&nbsp;°C (84–86&nbsp;°F) in March, the hottest month in the rainy season (called kashkazi/kaskazi [meaning north monsoon], which runs from November to April), and an average low of 19&nbsp;°C (66&nbsp;°F) in the cool, dry season (kusi (meaning south monsoon), which proceeds from May to October).<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[46]</a></sup> The islands are rarely subject to <a href="/wiki/Cyclone" title="Cyclone">cyclones</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ecology_and_environment">Ecology and environment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comoros&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Ecology and environment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Moheli_Marine_Park" title="Moheli Marine Park">Moheli Marine Park</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The Comoros constitute an <a href="/wiki/Ecoregion" title="Ecoregion">ecoregion</a> in their own right, <a href="/wiki/Comoros_forests" title="Comoros forests">Comoros forests</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[47]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-DinersteinOlson2017_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DinersteinOlson2017-50">[48]</a></sup> It had a 2018 <a href="/wiki/Forest_Landscape_Integrity_Index" title="Forest Landscape Integrity Index">Forest Landscape Integrity Index</a> mean score of 7.69/10, ranking it 33<sup>rd</sup> globally out of 172 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-FLII-Supplementary_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FLII-Supplementary-51">[49]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In December 1952 a specimen of the <a href="/wiki/Coelacanth" title="Coelacanth">coelacanth</a> fish was re-discovered off the Comoros coast. The 66 million-year-old species was thought to have been long extinct until its first recorded appearance in 1938 off the South African coast.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[50]</a></sup> Between 1938 and 1975, 84 specimens were caught and recorded.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[51]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government">Government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comoros&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_the_Comoros" title="Politics of the Comoros">Politics of the Comoros</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Moroni_harbour_(2).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Moroni_harbour_%282%29.jpg/220px-Moroni_harbour_%282%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Moroni_harbour_%282%29.jpg/330px-Moroni_harbour_%282%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Moroni_harbour_%282%29.jpg/440px-Moroni_harbour_%282%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2816" data-file-height="2112"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Moroni_harbour_(2).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Moroni,_Comoros" title="Moroni, Comoros">Moroni</a>, capital of the Comoros, with the port and Badjanani Mosque
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Politics of the Comoros takes place in a framework of a <a href="/wiki/Federation" title="Federation">federal</a> <a href="/wiki/Presidential_system" title="Presidential system">presidential</a> <a href="/wiki/Republic" title="Republic">republic</a>, whereby the <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_Comoros" class="mw-redirect" title="President of the Comoros">President of the Comoros</a> is both <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a> and <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">head of government</a>, and of a <a href="/wiki/Multi-party_system" title="Multi-party system">multi-party system</a>. The Constitution of the Union of the Comoros was ratified by referendum on 23 December 2001, and the islands' constitutions and executives were elected in the following months. It had previously been considered a military dictatorship, and the transfer of power from Azali Assoumani to Ahmed Abdallah Mohamed Sambi in May 2006 was a watershed moment as it was the first peaceful transfer in Comorian history. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Executive_power" class="mw-redirect" title="Executive power">Executive power</a> is exercised by the government. Federal <a href="/wiki/Legislative_power" class="mw-redirect" title="Legislative power">legislative power</a> is vested in both the <a href="/wiki/Forms_of_government" class="mw-redirect" title="Forms of government">government</a> and parliament. The preamble of the constitution guarantees an Islamic inspiration in governance, a commitment to human rights, and several specific enumerated rights, democracy, "a common destiny" for all Comorians.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[52]</a></sup> Each of the islands (according to Title II of the Constitution) has a great amount of autonomy in the Union, including having their own constitutions (or Fundamental Law), president, and Parliament. The presidency and Assembly of the Union are distinct from each of the islands' governments. The presidency of the Union rotates between the islands.<sup id="cite_ref-CfHR_Law-of-the-Union_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CfHR_Law-of-the-Union-55">[53]</a></sup> Despite widespread misgivings about the durability of the system of presidential rotation, Ngazidja holds the current presidency rotation, and Azali is President of the Union; Ndzuani is in theory to provide the next president.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[54]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Legal_system">Legal system</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comoros&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Legal system">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The Comorian <a href="/wiki/Legal_system" class="mw-redirect" title="Legal system">legal system</a> rests on <a href="/wiki/Islamic#Law" class="mw-redirect" title="Islamic">Islamic law</a>, an inherited French (<a href="/wiki/Napoleonic_Code" title="Napoleonic Code">Napoleonic Code</a>) legal code, and customary law (mila na ntsi). Village elders, kadis or civilian courts settle most disputes. The <a href="/wiki/Judiciary" title="Judiciary">judiciary</a> is independent of the <a href="/wiki/Legislative" class="mw-redirect" title="Legislative">legislative</a> and the executive. The Supreme Court acts as a Constitutional Council in resolving constitutional questions and supervising presidential elections. As High Court of Justice, the Supreme Court also arbitrates in cases where the government is accused of malpractice. The Supreme Court consists of two members selected by the president, two elected by the Federal Assembly, and one by the council of each island.<sup id="cite_ref-CfHR_Law-of-the-Union_55-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CfHR_Law-of-the-Union-55">[53]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_culture">Political culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comoros&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Political culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Around 80 percent of the central government's annual budget is spent on the country's complex administrative system which provides for a semi-autonomous government and president for each of the three islands and a rotating presidency for the overarching Union government.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[55]</a></sup> A referendum took place on 16 May 2009 to decide whether to cut down the government's unwieldy political bureaucracy. 52.7% of those eligible voted, and 93.8% of votes were cast in approval of the referendum. Following the implementation of the changes, each island's president became a governor and the ministers became councillors.<sup id="cite_ref-allafrica20090519_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-allafrica20090519-58">[56]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comoros&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Foreign relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_the_Comoros" title="Foreign relations of the Comoros">Foreign relations of the Comoros</a>
      </div> 
      <p>In November 1975, the Comoros became the 143rd member of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>. The new nation was defined as comprising the entire <a href="/wiki/Archipelago" title="Archipelago">archipelago</a>, although the citizens of <a href="/wiki/Mayotte" title="Mayotte">Mayotte</a> chose to become French citizens and keep their island as a French territory.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[57]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Comoros has repeatedly pressed its claim to Mayotte before the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly" title="United Nations General Assembly">United Nations General Assembly</a>, which adopted a series of resolutions under the caption "Question of the Comorian Island of Mayotte", opining that Mayotte belongs to the Comoros under the principle that the territorial integrity of colonial territories should be preserved upon independence. As a practical matter, however, these resolutions have little effect and there is no foreseeable likelihood that Mayotte will become <i>de facto</i> part of the Comoros without its people's consent. More recently, the Assembly has maintained this item on its agenda but deferred it from year to year without taking action. Other bodies, including the <a href="/wiki/Organization_of_African_Unity" class="mw-redirect" title="Organization of African Unity">Organization of African Unity</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Non-Aligned_Movement" title="Non-Aligned Movement">Movement of Non-Aligned Countries</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_of_Islamic_Cooperation" title="Organisation of Islamic Cooperation">Organisation of Islamic Cooperation</a>, have similarly questioned French sovereignty over Mayotte.<sup id="cite_ref-GA31_first-resolution_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GA31_first-resolution-9">[7]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[58]</a></sup> To close the debate and to avoid being integrated by force in the Union of the Comoros, the population of Mayotte overwhelmingly chose to become an <a href="/wiki/Overseas_department" class="mw-redirect" title="Overseas department">overseas department</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Region_of_France" class="mw-redirect" title="Region of France">region of France</a> in a <a href="/wiki/2009_Mahoran_status_referendum" title="2009 Mahoran status referendum">2009 referendum</a>. The new status was effective on 31 March 2011 and Mayotte has been recognised as an <a href="/wiki/Outermost_region" class="mw-redirect" title="Outermost region">outermost region</a> by the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> on 1 January 2014. This decision legally integrates Mayotte in the <a href="/wiki/French_Republic" class="mw-redirect" title="French Republic">French Republic</a>. </p>
      <p>The Comoros is a member of the <a href="/wiki/African_Union" title="African Union">African Union</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Arab_League" title="Arab League">Arab League</a>, the <a href="/wiki/European_Development_Fund" title="European Development Fund">European Development Fund</a>, the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a>, the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Ocean_Commission" title="Indian Ocean Commission">Indian Ocean Commission</a> and the <a href="/wiki/African_Development_Bank" title="African Development Bank">African Development Bank</a>. On 10 April 2008, the Comoros became the 179th nation to accept the <a href="/wiki/Kyoto_Protocol" title="Kyoto Protocol">Kyoto Protocol</a> to the United Nations Framework Convention on Climate Change.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[59]</a></sup> The Comoros signed the UN <a href="/wiki/Treaty_on_the_Prohibition_of_Nuclear_Weapons" title="Treaty on the Prohibition of Nuclear Weapons">treaty on the Prohibition of Nuclear Weapons</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[60]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In May 2013 the Union of the Comoros became known for filing a referral to the Office of the Prosecutor of the International Criminal Court (ICC) regarding the events of "the 31 May 2010 Israeli raid on the Humanitarian Aid Flotilla bound for [the] Gaza Strip". In November 2014 the ICC Prosecutor eventually decided<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[61]</a></sup> that the events did constitute war crimes but did not meet the gravity standards of bringing the case before ICC.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[62]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The emigration rate of skilled workers was about 21.2% in 2000.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[63]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comoros&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Military_of_the_Comoros" title="Military of the Comoros">Military of the Comoros</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The military resources of the Comoros consist of a small standing army and a 500-member police force, as well as a 500-member defence force. A defence treaty with France provides naval resources for protection of territorial waters, training of Comorian military personnel, and air surveillance. France maintains a few senior officers presence in the Comoros at government request. France maintains a small maritime base and a <a href="/wiki/French_Foreign_Legion" title="French Foreign Legion">Foreign Legion</a> Detachment (DLEM) on <a href="/wiki/Mayotte" title="Mayotte">Mayotte</a>. </p>
      <p>Once the new government was installed in May–June 2011, an expert mission from UNREC (Lomé) came to the Comoros and produced guidelines for the elaboration of a national security policy, which were discussed by different actors, notably the national defence authorities and civil society.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[64]</a></sup> By the end of the programme in end March 2012, a normative framework agreed upon by all entities involved in SSR will have been established. This will then have to be adopted by Parliament and implemented by the authorities. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_rights">Human rights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comoros&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Human rights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_the_Comoros" title="Human rights in the Comoros">Human rights in the Comoros</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Both male and female <a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_the_Comoros" title="LGBT rights in the Comoros">same-sex sexual acts</a> are illegal in Comoros.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[65]</a></sup> Such acts are punished with up to five years imprisonment.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[66]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comoros&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_the_Comoros" title="Economy of the Comoros">Economy of the Comoros</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Tree_map_export_2009_Comoros.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Tree_map_export_2009_Comoros.jpeg/350px-Tree_map_export_2009_Comoros.jpeg" decoding="async" width="350" height="273" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Tree_map_export_2009_Comoros.jpeg/525px-Tree_map_export_2009_Comoros.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Tree_map_export_2009_Comoros.jpeg/700px-Tree_map_export_2009_Comoros.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="1107" data-file-height="865"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Tree_map_export_2009_Comoros.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A proportional representation of the Comoros's exports
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The level of <a href="/wiki/Poverty" title="Poverty">poverty</a> in the Comoros is high, but "judging by the <a href="/wiki/Poverty_threshold" title="Poverty threshold">international poverty threshold</a> of $1.9 per person per day, only two out of every ten Comorians could be classified as poor, a rate that places the Comoros ahead of other <a href="/wiki/Low-income_countries" class="mw-redirect" title="Low-income countries">low-income countries</a> and 30 percentage points ahead of other countries in <a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africa" title="Sub-Saharan Africa">Sub-Saharan Africa</a>."<sup id="cite_ref-2018WorldBank_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2018WorldBank-69">[67]</a></sup> Poverty declined by about 10% between 2014 and 2018, and living conditions generally improved.<sup id="cite_ref-2018WorldBank_69-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2018WorldBank-69">[67]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Economic_inequality" title="Economic inequality">Economic inequality</a> remains widespread, with a major gap between rural and urban areas.<sup id="cite_ref-2018WorldBank_69-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2018WorldBank-69">[67]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Remittance" title="Remittance">Remittances</a> through the sizable Comorian diaspora form a substantial part of the country's GDP<sup id="cite_ref-CSIS_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CSIS-70">[68]</a></sup> and have contributed to decreases in poverty and increases in living standards.<sup id="cite_ref-2018WorldBank_69-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2018WorldBank-69">[67]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>According to <a href="/wiki/ILO" class="mw-redirect" title="ILO">ILO</a>'s ILOSTAT statistical database, between 1991 and 2019 the <a href="/wiki/Unemployment_rate" class="mw-redirect" title="Unemployment rate">unemployment rate</a> as a percent of the total labor force ranged from 4.38% to 4.3%.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[69]</a></sup> An October 2005 paper by the Comoros Ministry of Planning and Regional Development, however, reported that "registered unemployment rate is 14.3 percent, distributed very unevenly among and within the islands, but with marked incidence in urban areas."<sup id="cite_ref-Office_of_the_General_Commissioner_for_Planning,_Ministry_of_Planning_and_Regional_Development_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Office_of_the_General_Commissioner_for_Planning,_Ministry_of_Planning_and_Regional_Development-72">[70]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2019, more than 56% of the labor force was employed in agriculture, with 29% employed in industry and 14% employed in services.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[71]</a></sup> The islands' agricultural sector is based on the export of <a href="/wiki/Spice" title="Spice">spices</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Vanilla" title="Vanilla">vanilla</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cinnamon" title="Cinnamon">cinnamon</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Cloves" class="mw-redirect" title="Cloves">cloves</a>, and thus susceptible to price fluctuations in the volatile world <a href="/wiki/Commodity_market" title="Commodity market">commodity market</a> for these goods.<sup id="cite_ref-CSIS_70-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CSIS-70">[68]</a></sup> The Comoros is the world's largest producer of <a href="/wiki/Ylang-ylang" class="mw-redirect" title="Ylang-ylang">ylang-ylang</a>, a plant whose extracted <a href="/wiki/Essential_oil" title="Essential oil">essential oil</a> is used in the <a href="/wiki/Perfume" title="Perfume">perfume</a> industry; some 80% of the world's supply comes from the Comoros.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[72]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>High population densities, as much as 1000 per square kilometre in the densest agricultural zones, for what is still a mostly rural, agricultural economy may lead to an environmental crisis in the near future, especially considering the high rate of population growth. In 2004 the Comoros' real GDP growth was a low 1.9% and real GDP per capita continued to decline. These declines are explained by factors including declining investment, drops in consumption, rising inflation, and an increase in trade imbalance due in part to lowered cash crop prices, especially vanilla.<sup id="cite_ref-Office_of_the_General_Commissioner_for_Planning,_Ministry_of_Planning_and_Regional_Development_72-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Office_of_the_General_Commissioner_for_Planning,_Ministry_of_Planning_and_Regional_Development-72">[70]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Fiscal policy is constrained by erratic fiscal revenues, a bloated civil service wage bill, and an external debt that is far above the <a href="/wiki/Heavily_indebted_poor_countries" title="Heavily indebted poor countries">HIPC</a> threshold. Membership in the franc zone, the main anchor of stability, has nevertheless helped contain pressures on domestic prices.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[73]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Comoros has an inadequate transportation system, a young and rapidly increasing population, and few natural resources. The low educational level of the labour force contributes to a subsistence level of economic activity, high <a href="/wiki/Unemployment" title="Unemployment">unemployment</a>, and a heavy dependence on foreign grants and technical assistance. Agriculture contributes 40% to <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">GDP</a> and provides most of the exports. </p>
      <p>The government is struggling to upgrade education and technical training, to privatise commercial and industrial enterprises, to improve health services, to diversify exports, to promote tourism, and to reduce the high population growth rate.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[74]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Comoros is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Organization_for_the_Harmonization_of_Business_Law_in_Africa" class="mw-redirect" title="Organization for the Harmonization of Business Law in Africa">Organization for the Harmonization of Business Law in Africa</a> (<a href="/wiki/OHADA" title="OHADA">OHADA</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-ohada.com_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ohada.com-77">[75]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comoros&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_the_Comoros" title="Demographics of the Comoros">Demographics of the Comoros</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Moroni_Mosque_Photo_by_Sascha_Grabow.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Moroni_Mosque_Photo_by_Sascha_Grabow.jpg/170px-Moroni_Mosque_Photo_by_Sascha_Grabow.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="232" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Moroni_Mosque_Photo_by_Sascha_Grabow.jpg/255px-Moroni_Mosque_Photo_by_Sascha_Grabow.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Moroni_Mosque_Photo_by_Sascha_Grabow.jpg/340px-Moroni_Mosque_Photo_by_Sascha_Grabow.jpg 2x" data-file-width="594" data-file-height="812"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Moroni_Mosque_Photo_by_Sascha_Grabow.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A mosque in Moroni
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <table class="wikitable" style="float: right; margin-left: 10px"> 
       <caption>
        Population in Comoros<sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-7">[5]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_2019_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP_2019-8">[6]</a></sup> 
       </caption> 
       <tbody>
        <tr> 
         <th scope="col" style="background:#cfb;">Year </th> 
         <th scope="col" style="background:#cfb;">Million </th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td>1950</td> 
         <td style="text-align:right;">0.16 </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td>2000</td> 
         <td style="text-align:right;">0.54 </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td>2018</td> 
         <td style="text-align:right;">0.8 </td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <p>With fewer than a million people, the Comoros is one of the least populous countries in the world, but is also one of the most densely populated, with an average of 275 inhabitants per square kilometre (710/sq&nbsp;mi). In 2001, 34% of the population was considered urban, but that is expected to grow, since rural population growth is negative, while overall population growth is still relatively high.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[76]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Almost half the population of the Comoros is under the age of 15.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[77]</a></sup> Major urban centres include <a href="/wiki/Moroni,_Comoros" title="Moroni, Comoros">Moroni</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mitsamihuli&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Mitsamihuli (page does not exist)">Mitsamihuli</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Fumbuni&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Fumbuni (page does not exist)">Fumbuni</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mutsamudu" title="Mutsamudu">Mutsamudu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Domoni" title="Domoni">Domoni</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Fomboni" title="Fomboni">Fomboni</a>. There are between 200,000 and 350,000 Comorians in France.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[78]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnic_groups">Ethnic groups</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comoros&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Ethnic groups">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The islands of the Comoros share mostly African-Arab origins. Minorities include <a href="/wiki/Malagasy_people" title="Malagasy people">Malagasy</a> (Christian) and <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_Groups_of_South_Asia" class="mw-redirect" title="Ethnic Groups of South Asia">Indian</a> (mostly <a href="/wiki/Ismaili" class="mw-redirect" title="Ismaili">Ismaili</a>). There are recent immigrants of <a href="/wiki/Chinese_people" title="Chinese people">Chinese</a> origin in Grande Comore (especially Moroni). Although most French left after independence in 1975, a small <a href="/wiki/Creole_peoples" title="Creole peoples">Creole</a> community, descended from settlers from France, Madagascar and Réunion, lives in the Comoros.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comoros&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_the_Comoros" title="Languages of the Comoros">Languages of the Comoros</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The most common <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_the_Comoros" title="Languages of the Comoros">languages in the Comoros</a> are the <a href="/wiki/Comorian_languages" title="Comorian languages">Comorian languages</a>, collectively known <i>Shikomori</i>. They are related to <a href="/wiki/Swahili_language" title="Swahili language">Swahili</a>, and the four different variants (Shingazidja, Shimwali, Shindzuani and Shimaore) are spoken on each of the four islands. <a href="/wiki/Arabic_script" title="Arabic script">Arabic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Latin_script" title="Latin script">Latin</a> scripts are both used, Arabic being the more widely used, and an <a href="/wiki/Official_script" title="Official script">official orthography</a> has recently been developed for the Latin script.<sup id="cite_ref-chamanga_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chamanga-81">[79]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a> and <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a> are also official languages, along with Comorian. Arabic is widely known as a second language, being the language of Quranic teaching. French is the administrative language and the language of most non-Quranic formal education. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comoros&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_the_Comoros" title="Religion in the Comoros">Religion in the Comoros</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Anjouan_-_Islands_of_Comoros.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Anjouan_-_Islands_of_Comoros.jpg/220px-Anjouan_-_Islands_of_Comoros.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="157" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Anjouan_-_Islands_of_Comoros.jpg/330px-Anjouan_-_Islands_of_Comoros.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Anjouan_-_Islands_of_Comoros.jpg/440px-Anjouan_-_Islands_of_Comoros.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1463"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Anjouan_-_Islands_of_Comoros.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A view of Domoni, <a href="/wiki/Anjouan" title="Anjouan">Anjouan</a> including mosque
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Sunni_Islam" title="Sunni Islam">Sunni Islam</a> is <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_the_Comoros" title="Islam in the Comoros">the dominant religion</a>, followed by as much as 99% of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[80]</a></sup> Comoros is the only Muslim-majority country in Southern Africa and the second southernmost Muslim-majority territory after the French territory of <a href="/wiki/Mayotte" title="Mayotte">Mayotte</a>. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism_in_the_Comoros" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholicism in the Comoros">A minority of the population</a> of the Comoros are Christian, both Catholic and Protestant denominations are represented, and most Malagasy residents are also Christian. Expatriates from metropolitan France are mostly <a href="/wiki/Catholic" class="mw-redirect" title="Catholic">Catholic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[81]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comoros&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Health_in_the_Comoros" title="Health in the Comoros">Health in the Comoros</a>
      </div> 
      <p>There are 15 physicians per 100,000 people. The <a href="/wiki/Fertility_rate" class="mw-redirect" title="Fertility rate">fertility rate</a> was 4.7 per adult woman in 2004. <a href="/wiki/Life_expectancy" title="Life expectancy">Life expectancy</a> at birth is 67 for females and 62 for males.<sup id="cite_ref-afro.who.int_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-afro.who.int-84">[82]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comoros&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_the_Comoros" title="Education in the Comoros">Education in the Comoros</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Almost all children attend <a href="/wiki/Quranic_school" class="mw-redirect" title="Quranic school">Quranic schools</a>, usually before, although increasingly in tandem with regular schooling. Children are taught about the <a href="/wiki/Qur%27an" class="mw-redirect" title="Qur'an">Qur'an</a>, and memorise it, and learn the Arabic script. Most parents prefer their children to attend Koran schools before moving on to the French-based schooling system. Although the state sector is plagued by a lack of resources, and the teachers by unpaid salaries, there are numerous private and community schools of relatively good standard. The national curriculum, apart from a few years during the revolutionary period immediately post-independence, has been very much based on the French system, both because resources are French and most Comorians hope to go on to further education in France. There have recently been moves to Comorianise the syllabus and integrate the two systems, the formal and the Quran schools, into one, thus moving away from the secular educational system inherited from France.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[83]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Pre-colonization education systems in Comoros focused on necessary skills such as agriculture, caring for livestock and completing household tasks. Religious education also taught children the virtues of Islam. The education system underwent a transformation during colonization in the early 1900s which brought secular education based on the French system. This was mainly for children of the elite. After Comoros gained independence in 1975, the education system changed again. Funding for teachers' salaries was lost, and many went on strike. Thus, the public education system was not functioning between 1997 and 2001. Since gaining independence, the education system has also undergone a democratization and options exist for those other than the elite. Enrollment has also grown. </p>
      <p>In 2000, 44.2% of children ages 5 to 14 years were attending school. There is a general lack of facilities, equipment, qualified teachers, textbooks and other resources. <a href="/wiki/Salaries" class="mw-redirect" title="Salaries">Salaries</a> for teachers are often so far in arrears that many refuse to work.<sup id="cite_ref-ilab_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ilab-86">[84]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Prior to 2000, students seeking a university education had to attend school outside of the country, however in the early 2000s a university was created in the country. This served to help economic growth and to fight the "flight" of many educated people who were not returning to the islands to work.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[85]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>About fifty-seven percent of the population is literate in the <a href="/wiki/Latin_script" title="Latin script">Latin script</a> while more than 90% are literate in the <a href="/wiki/Arabic_script" title="Arabic script">Arabic script</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[86]</a></sup> Comorian has no native script, but both Arabic and Latin scripts are used. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comoros&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Public_holidays_in_the_Comoros" title="Public holidays in the Comoros">Public holidays in the Comoros</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Traditionally, women on Ndzuani wear red and white patterned garments called <i>shiromani</i>, while on Ngazidja and Mwali colourful shawls called <i>leso</i> are worn. Many women apply a paste of ground <a href="/wiki/Sandalwood" title="Sandalwood">sandalwood</a> and <a href="/wiki/Coral" title="Coral">coral</a> called <i>msinzano</i> to their faces.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[87]</a></sup> Traditional male clothing is a long white shirt known as a <i>nkandu</i>, and a bonnet called a <i>kofia</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[88]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Marriage">Marriage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comoros&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Marriage">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>There are two types of marriages in Comoros, the little marriage (known as <i>Mna daho</i> on Ngazidja) and the customary marriage (known as <i>ada</i> on Ngazidja, <i>harusi</i> on the other islands). The little marriage is a simple legal marriage. It is small, intimate, and inexpensive and the bride's dowry is nominal. A man may undertake a number of <i>Mna daho</i> marriages in his lifetime, often at the same time, a woman fewer; but both men and women will usually only undertake one <i>ada</i>, or grand marriage, and this must generally be within the village. The hallmarks of the grand marriage are dazzling gold jewelry, two weeks of celebration and an enormous bridal dowry. Although the expenses are shared between both families as well as with a wider social circle, an ada wedding on Ngazidja can cost up to €50,000 (74,000 US dollars). Many couples take a lifetime to save for their ada, and it is not uncommon for a marriage to be attended by a couple's adult children.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[89]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <i>ada</i> marriage marks a man's transition in the Ngazidja age system from youth to elder. His status in the social hierarchy greatly increases, and he will henceforth be entitled to speak in public and participate in the political process, both in his village and more widely across the island. He will be entitled to display his status by wearing a <i>mharuma</i>, a type of shawl, across his shoulders, and he can enter the mosque by the door reserved for elders, and sit at the front. A woman's status also changes, although less formally, as she becomes a "mother" and moves into her own house. The system is less formalised on the other islands, but the marriage is nevertheless a significant and costly event across the archipelago. </p>
      <p>The <i>ada</i> is often criticized because of its great expense, but at the same time it is a source of social cohesion and the main reason why migrants in France and elsewhere continue to send money home. Increasingly, marriages are also being taxed for the purposes of village development.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[90]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Kinship_and_social_structure">Kinship and social structure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comoros&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Kinship and social structure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:JOUR_DE_L%27A%C3%8FDE_DHUL_HAJJ_BANGOI-KOUNI.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/JOUR_DE_L%27A%C3%8FDE_DHUL_HAJJ_BANGOI-KOUNI.jpg/220px-JOUR_DE_L%27A%C3%8FDE_DHUL_HAJJ_BANGOI-KOUNI.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/JOUR_DE_L%27A%C3%8FDE_DHUL_HAJJ_BANGOI-KOUNI.jpg/330px-JOUR_DE_L%27A%C3%8FDE_DHUL_HAJJ_BANGOI-KOUNI.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/JOUR_DE_L%27A%C3%8FDE_DHUL_HAJJ_BANGOI-KOUNI.jpg/440px-JOUR_DE_L%27A%C3%8FDE_DHUL_HAJJ_BANGOI-KOUNI.jpg 2x" data-file-width="960" data-file-height="540"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:JOUR_DE_L%27A%C3%8FDE_DHUL_HAJJ_BANGOI-KOUNI.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Villagers in Bangwa Kuuni, Ngazidja
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Comorian society has a <a href="/wiki/Bilateral_descent" title="Bilateral descent">bilateral descent</a> system. Lineage membership and inheritance of immovable goods (land, housing) is matrilineal, passed in the maternal line, similar to many <a href="/wiki/Bantu_peoples" title="Bantu peoples">Bantu peoples</a> who are also matrilineal, while other goods and patronymics are passed in the male line. However, there are differences between the islands, the matrilineal element being stronger on Ngazidja.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[91]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comoros&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_the_Comoro_Islands" class="mw-redirect" title="Music of the Comoro Islands">Music of the Comoro Islands</a>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/w/index.php?title=Twarab&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Twarab (page does not exist)">Twarab</a> music, imported from <a href="/wiki/Zanzibar" title="Zanzibar">Zanzibar</a> in the early 20th century, remains the most influential genre on the islands and is popular at <i>ada</i> marriages.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[92]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comoros&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Media_of_the_Comoros" class="mw-redirect" title="Media of the Comoros">Media of the Comoros</a>
      </div> 
      <p>There are two daily national <a href="/wiki/Newspaper" title="Newspaper">newspapers</a> published in the Comoros, the government-owned <i><a href="/wiki/Al-Watwan" title="Al-Watwan">Al-Watwan</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[93]</a></sup> and the privately owned <i>La Gazette des Comores</i>, both published in <a href="/wiki/Moroni,_Comoros" title="Moroni, Comoros">Moroni</a>. There are a number of smaller newsletters published on an irregular basis as well as a variety of news websites. The government-owned ORTC provides national radio and television service and there are a number of privately owned stations broadcasting locally in the larger towns.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comoros&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

           <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"><cite class="citation web cs1"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://population.un.org/wpp/">"<span class="cs1-kern-left">"</span>World Population prospects – Population division<span class="cs1-kern-right">"</span>"</a>. <i>population.un.org</i>. <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Department_of_Economic_and_Social_Affairs" title="United Nations Department of Economic and Social Affairs">United Nations Department of Economic and Social Affairs</a>, Population Division<span class="reference-accessdate">.          <li id="cite_note-UN_WPP_2019-8"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-UN_WPP_2019_8-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-UN_WPP_2019_8-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">
           <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"><cite class="citation web cs1"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://population.un.org/wpp/Download/Files/1_Indicators%20(Standard)/EXCEL_FILES/1_Population/WPP2019_POP_F01_1_TOTAL_POPULATION_BOTH_SEXES.xlsx">"<span class="cs1-kern-left">"</span>Overall total population" – World Population Prospects: The 2019 Revision"</a> <span class="cs1-format">(xslx)</span>. <i>population.un.org</i> (custom data acquired via website). <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Department_of_Economic_and_Social_Affairs" title="United Nations Department of Economic and Social Affairs">United Nations Department of Economic and Social Affairs</a>, Population Division<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">9 November</span> 2019</span>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.jtitle=population.un.org&amp;rft.atitle=%22Overall+total+population%22+%E2%80%93+World+Population+Prospects%3A+The+2019+Revision&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fpopulation.un.org%2Fwpp%2FDownload%2FFiles%2F1_Indicators%2520%28Standard%29%2FEXCEL_FILES%2F1_Population%2FWPP2019_POP_F01_1_TOTAL_POPULATION_BOTH_SEXES.xlsx&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AComoros" class="Z3988"></span></span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-GA31_first-resolution-9"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-GA31_first-resolution_9-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-GA31_first-resolution_9-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">The first UN General Assembly Resolution regarding the matter, "<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20080408191407/http://un.cti.depaul.edu/Countries/Comoros/1156213396.pdf">Question of the Comorian island of Mayotte</a> (PDF)", United Nations General Assembly Resolution A/RES/31/4, (21 October 1976) states "the occupation by France of the Comorian island of Mayotte constitutes a flagrant encroachment on the national unity of the Comorian State, a Member of the United Nations," rejecting the French-administered referendums and condemning French presence in Mayotte.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-10"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-10">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">As defined by the <a href="/wiki/Organization_of_African_Unity" class="mw-redirect" title="Organization of African Unity">Organization of African Unity</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Non-Aligned_Movement" title="Non-Aligned Movement">Movement of Non-Aligned Countries</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_of_Islamic_Cooperation" title="Organisation of Islamic Cooperation">Organisation of Islamic Cooperation</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly" title="United Nations General Assembly">United Nations General Assembly</a>: the most recent UN General Assembly Resolution regarding the matter, "Question of the Comorian island of Mayotte," United Nations General Assembly Resolution A/RES/49/18, (6 December 1994) states "the results of the referendum of 22 December 1974 were to be considered on a global basis and not island by island,...Reaffirms the sovereignty of the Islamic Federal Republic of the Comoros over the island of Mayotte". <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20080106080523/http://un.cti.depaul.edu/public/Comoros/10/English/">Several resolutions expressing similar sentiments were passed between 1977 (31/4) and 1994 (49/18).</a></span> </li>
